	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Crimea</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Crimea.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Crimea.svg/220px-Flag_of_Crimea.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Crimea.svg/330px-Flag_of_Crimea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Flag_of_Crimea.svg/440px-Flag_of_Crimea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Crimea.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Flag of Crimea republic (<i><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">de jure</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">de facto</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a>, depending on jurisdiction) used under Russia and Ukraine</div></div></div>
<p><b>Crimea</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Крым</span>; <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Крим</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Ukrainian" title="Romanization of Ukrainian">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="uk-Latn" title="Ukrainian-language romanization">Krym</i>; <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>: <span lang="crh">Къырым</span>, <small>romanized:&#160;</small><i lang="crh-Latn" title="Crimean Tatar-language romanization">Kirim/Qırım</i>; <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">Κιμμερία/Ταυρική</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Ancient_Greek" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanization of Ancient Greek">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="grc-Latn" title="Ancient Greek-language romanization">Kimmería/Taurikḗ</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> on the northern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> that is almost completely surrounded by both the Black Sea and the smaller <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a> to the northeast. It is located south of the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Kherson_Oblast" title="Kherson Oblast">Kherson</a>, to which it is connected by the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">Isthmus of Perekop</a>, and west of the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Kuban" title="Kuban">Kuban</a>, from which it is separated by the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Kerch" class="mw-redirect" title="Strait of Kerch">Strait of Kerch</a> though linked by the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Bridge" title="Crimean Bridge">Crimean Bridge</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Arabat_Spit" title="Arabat Spit">Arabat Spit</a> is located to the northeast, a narrow strip of land that separates a system of lagoons named <a href="/wiki/Sivash" class="mw-redirect" title="Sivash">Sivash</a> from the Sea of Azov. Across the Black Sea to its west is <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and to its south <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.
</p><p>Crimea (or <b>Tauric Peninsula</b>, as it was called from <a href="/wiki/History_of_Crimea#Antiquity" title="History of Crimea">antiquity</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>) has historically been at the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical world</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pontic%E2%80%93Caspian_steppe" title="Pontic–Caspian steppe">Pontic–Caspian steppe</a>. Its southern fringe was colonised by the <a href="/wiki/Greek_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek colonies">Greeks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Crimea">Romans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cherson_(theme)" title="Cherson (theme)">Byzantine Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Theodoro" title="Principality of Theodoro">Crimean Goths</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, while at the same time its interior was occupied by a changing cast of invading <a href="/wiki/Steppe_nomads" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppe nomads">steppe nomads</a> and empires, such as the <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. Crimea and adjacent territories were united in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a> during the 15th to 18th century.
</p><p>In 1783, Crimea <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire">was annexed</a> by the Russian Empire as the result of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)">Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917, Crimea became an <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">autonomous republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">USSR</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Crimea was downgraded to the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Oblast" title="Crimean Oblast">Crimean Oblast</a> after its entire indigenous population, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">were deported to Central Asia</a>, an act recognized as a genocide. In 1954, it was <a href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">transferred to the Ukrainian SSR</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the collapse of the Soviet Union, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> was reestablished as an independent state in 1991, and most of the peninsula was reorganized as the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a>, while the city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> retained its special status within Ukraine. The 1997 <a href="/wiki/Partition_Treaty_on_the_Status_and_Conditions_of_the_Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet">Partition Treaty on the Status and Conditions of the Black Sea Fleet</a> partitioned the former Soviet Black Sea Fleet and allowed Russia to continue basing its fleet in Crimea: both the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Naval_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian Naval Forces">Ukrainian Naval Forces</a> and Russian's Black Sea Fleet were to be headquartered in Sevastopol. Ukraine extended Russia's lease of the naval facilities under the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv_Pact" title="Kharkiv Pact">Kharkiv Pact</a> in exchange for further discounted <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>.
</p><p>In February 2014, following the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a> that ousted the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">Ukrainian President</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a>, pro-Russian separatists and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Russian Armed Forces</a> <a href="/wiki/2014_Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Russian military intervention in Ukraine">took over the territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> A controversial <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Crimean referendum">Crimea-wide referendum</a>, unconstitutional under the Ukrainian and Crimean constitutions,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> was held on the issue of reunification with Russia, which official results indicated was supported by a large majority of Crimeans.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian20140317_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian20140317-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Russia  formally <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexed</a> Crimea on 18 March 2014, incorporating the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_city" title="Federal city">federal city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> as the 84th and 85th <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<p>The classical name <i><a href="/wiki/History_of_Crimea#Antiquity" title="History of Crimea">Tauris</a></i> or <i>Taurica</i> is from the Greek Ταυρική (Taurikḗ), after the peninsula's Scytho-Cimmerian inhabitants, the <a href="/wiki/Tauri" title="Tauri">Tauri</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> (<i>Geography</i> vii 4.3, xi. 2.5), <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a>, (<i>Histories</i> 4.39.4), and <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> (<i>Geographia</i>. II, v 9.5) refer variously to the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Kerch" class="mw-redirect" title="Strait of Kerch">Strait of Kerch</a> as the Κιμμερικὸς Βόσπορος (<i>Kimmerikos Bosporos</i>, romanized spelling, <i>Bosporus Cimmerius</i>), its <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Peninsula" title="Kerch Peninsula">easternmost part</a> as the Κιμμέριον Ἄκρον (<i>Kimmerion Akron</i>, Roman name: Promontorium Cimmerium,<sup id="cite_ref-history1779_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history1779-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> as well as to the city of <a href="/wiki/Kimmerikon" title="Kimmerikon">Cimmerium</a> and whence the name of the <a href="/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom" title="Bosporan Kingdom">Kingdom of the Cimmerian Bosporus</a> (Κιμμερικοῦ Βοσπόρου).
</p><p>The earliest recorded use of the toponym “Crimea” for the peninsula<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> occurred between 1315-1329 AD by the Arab writer  <a href="/wiki/Abu%27l-Fida" title="Abu&#39;l-Fida">Abū al-Fidā</a> where he recounts a political fight in 1300-1301 AD resulting in a rival's decapitation and having “sent his head to the Crimea”.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a> name of the peninsula is Qırım (<a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>: <span lang="crh">Къырым</span>, <small>romanized:&#160;</small><i lang="crh-Latn" title="Crimean Tatar-language romanization">Kirim/Qırım</i>) and so also for the city of <i>Krym</i> which is now called <i><a href="/wiki/Stary_Krym" title="Stary Krym">Stary Krym</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> which served as a capital of the Crimean province of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. Some sources hold that the name of the capital was extended to the entire peninsula at some point during <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Ottoman suzerainty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The origin of the word <i>Qırım</i> is uncertain. Suggestions argued in various sources include:
</p>
<ol><li>a corruption of <i>Cimmerium</i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kimmerikon" title="Kimmerikon">Kimmerikon</a></i>, Κιμμερικόν).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>a derivation from the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic</a> term <i>qirum</i> ("fosse, trench"), from <i>qori-</i> ("to fence, protect").<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>Other suggestions either unsupported or contradicted by sources, apparently based on similarity in sound, include:
</p>
<ol><li>a derivation from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> <i>Cremnoi</i> (Κρημνοί, in post-classical <a href="/wiki/Koin%C3%A9_Greek" class="mw-redirect" title="Koiné Greek">Koiné Greek</a> pronunciation, <i>Crimni</i>, i.e., "the Cliffs", a port on <a href="/wiki/Maeotian_Swamp" title="Maeotian Swamp">Lake Maeotis</a> (Sea of Azov) cited by <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> in <i>The Histories</i> 4.20.1 and 4.110.2).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  However, Herodotus identifies the port not in Crimea, but as being on the west coast of the Sea of Azov. No evidence has been identified that this name was ever in use for the peninsula.</li>
<li>The Turkic term (e.g., in <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Kırım</i>) is related to the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a> appellation <i>kerm</i>  "wall", but sources indicate that the Mongolian appellation of the Crimean peninsula of <i>Qaram</i> is phonetically incompatible with <i>kerm/kerem</i> and therefore deriving from another original term.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>The name "Crimea" is the Italian form, i.e., <i>la Crimea</i>, since at least the 17th century<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and the "Crimean peninsula" becomes current during the 18th century, gradually replacing the classical name of <i>Tauric Peninsula</i> in the course of the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>   In English usage since the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a> the Crimean Khanate is referred to as <i>Crim Tartary</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The omission of the definite article in English ("Crimea" rather than "the Crimea") became common during the later 20th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The classical name was used in 1802 in the name of the Russian <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Taurida Governorate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> While it was replaced with <i>Krym</i> (<a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Крим</span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Крым</span>) in the Soviet Union and has had no official status since 1921, it is still used by some institutions in Crimea, such as the <a href="/wiki/Taurida_National_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Taurida National University">Taurida National University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FC_Tavriya_Simferopol" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Tavriya Simferopol">Tavriya Simferopol football club</a>, or the Tavrida federal highway.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Crimea" title="History of Crimea">History of Crimea</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">Ancient history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%96%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A5%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%C2%BB_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%96%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A5%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%C2%BB_2.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%96%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A5%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%C2%BB_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D1%96%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%96%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA_%C2%AB%D0%A5%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81_%D0%A2%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D1%96%D0%B9%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9%C2%BB_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruins of ancient Greek colony of <a href="/wiki/Chersonesus_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesus (Crimea)">Chersonesos</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg/330px-%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg/440px-%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3039" data-file-height="2014" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE_%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B4%D0%BE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Swallow%27s_Nest" title="Swallow&#39;s Nest">Swallow's Nest</a>, built in 1912 for businessman Baron Pavel von Steingel</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom" title="Bosporan Kingdom">Bosporan Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_pre-Roman_Crimea" title="Greeks in pre-Roman Crimea">Greeks in pre-Roman Crimea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Crimea">Roman Crimea</a></div>
<p>In the 8th century BC the <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a> migrated to the area in retreat from <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythian</a> advances, of whom the latter also migrated to the region.  Contemporaneously, and possibly because of the migration, the region came within the sphere of Greek maritime interest and became the site of <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_pre-Roman_Crimea" title="Greeks in pre-Roman Crimea">Greek colonies</a>. The most important Greek city was <a href="/wiki/Chersonesus_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesus (Crimea)">Chersonesos</a> at the edge of today's Sevastopol.
</p><p>The Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, under <a href="/wiki/Darius_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Darius I">Darius I</a>, expanded to Crimea as part of <a href="/wiki/European_Scythian_campaign_of_Darius_I" class="mw-redirect" title="European Scythian campaign of Darius I">his campaigns</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> in 513 BC.
</p><p>The peninsula, then under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom" title="Bosporan Kingdom">Bosporan Kingdom</a>, later became a client kingdom of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in 63 BC.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_history">Medieval history</span></h3>
<p>In the 9th century CE, Byzantium established the <a href="/wiki/Theme_of_Cherson" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme of Cherson">Theme of Cherson</a> to defend against incursions by the <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_Khaganate" title="Rus&#39; Khaganate">Rus' Khaganate</a>. The Crimean peninsula from this time was contested between Byzantium, Rus' and <a href="/wiki/Khazaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Khazaria">Khazaria</a>. The area remained the site of overlapping interests and contact between the early medieval Slavic, Turkic and Greek spheres. It became a center of <a href="/wiki/Saqaliba" title="Saqaliba">slave trade</a>. <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Slavs</a> were sold to Byzantium and other places in Anatolia and the Middle-East during this period.
</p>
<h3><span id="Mongol_Conquest_.281238-1449.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Mongol_Conquest_(1238-1449)">Mongol Conquest (1238-1449)</span></h3>
<p>Trapezuntine <a href="/wiki/Perateia" title="Perateia">Perateia</a> had already been subjected to pressure from the Genoese and Kipchaks by the time <a href="/wiki/Alexios_I_of_Trebizond" title="Alexios I of Trebizond">Alexios I of Trebizond</a> died in 1222 before the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol invasions">Mongol invasions</a> began its western swept through <a href="/wiki/Volga_Bulgaria" title="Volga Bulgaria">Volga Bulgaria</a> in 1223. With them, control of the peninsula changed in 1238, as all but the Perateia of Crimea was incorporated into the territory of the Golden Horde throughout the 14th century CE. In the course of the 13th century CE, portions were controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> and by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Republic of Genoa</a>, the Perateia soon became the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Theodoro" title="Principality of Theodoro">Principality of Theodoro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gazaria_(Genoese_colonies)" title="Gazaria (Genoese colonies)">Genoese Gazaria</a>, respectively.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg/220px-Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg/330px-Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg/440px-Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2133" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stary_Krym_Monastyr_Surb_Chacz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Armenian <a href="/wiki/Surp_Khach_Monastery" title="Surp Khach Monastery">monastery of the Holy Cross</a> (Սուրբ Խաչ, <i>Surb Khach</i>), established in 1358</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Crimean_Khanate_.281449.E2.80.931783.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_Khanate_(1449–1783)">Crimean Khanate (1449–1783)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Crimean-Nogai_raids_into_East_Slavic_lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands">Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Goths" title="Crimean Goths">Crimean Goths</a></div>
<p>The Crimean Khanate, a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Vassal state of the Ottoman Empire">vassal state of the Ottoman Empire</a>, succeeded the Golden Horde and lasted from 1449 to 1783.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1571, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Tatars</a> attacked and sacked Moscow, burning everything but the Kremlin.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Until the late 18th century, Crimean Tatars maintained a massive <a href="/wiki/Crimean-Nogai_raids_into_East_Slavic_lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands">slave trade</a> with the Ottoman Empire, exporting about 2 million slaves from Russia and Ukraine over the period 1500–1700.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Russian_Empire_.281783.E2.80.931917.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Empire_(1783–1917)">Russian Empire (1783–1917)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/New_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="New Russia">New Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Taurida Governorate</a></div>
<p>In 1774, the Khanate was proclaimed independent under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_K%C3%BC%C3%A7%C3%BCk_Kaynarca" title="Treaty of Küçük Kaynarca">Treaty of Küçük Kaynarca</a> with the Ottomans,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> but was then <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire">conquered by the Russian Empire in 1783</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GP223_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GP223-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Oblast" title="Taurida Oblast">Taurida Oblast</a> was created by a decree of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_II_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine II of Russia">Catherine the Great</a> on 2 February 1784. The center of the <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblast</a> was first in <a href="/wiki/Karasubazar" class="mw-redirect" title="Karasubazar">Karasubazar</a> but was moved to Simferopol later in 1784. The establishment decree divided the oblast into 7 <a href="/wiki/Uyezd" title="Uyezd">uyezds</a>. However, by a decree of <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul I</a> on 12 December 1796, the oblast was abolished and the territory, divided into 2 uyezds (Akmechetsky <i>[Акмечетский]</i> and Perekopsky <i>[Перекопский]</i>) was attached to the second incarnation of the <a href="/wiki/Novorossiysk_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Novorossiysk Governorate">Novorossiysk Governorate</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg/220px-Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg/330px-Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg/440px-Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="806" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_Sevastopol_by_George_Baxter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The eleven-month <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%9355)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854–55)">siege</a> of a Russian naval base at Sevastopol during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a></div></div></div>
<p>From 1853 to 1856, the peninsula was the site of the principal engagements of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>, a conflict fought between the Russian Empire and an alliance of <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Britain</a>, the Ottoman Empire and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Sardinia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Russian_Civil_War_.281917.E2.80.931921.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Civil_War_(1917–1921)">Russian Civil War (1917–1921)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_People%27s_Republic" title="Crimean People&#39;s Republic">Crimean People's Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Taurida Soviet Socialist Republic">Taurida Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Regional_Government" title="Crimean Regional Government">Crimean Regional Government</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Socialist_Soviet_Republic" title="Crimean Socialist Soviet Republic">Crimean Socialist Soviet Republic</a></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">Russian Revolution of 1917</a>, the military and political situation in Crimea was chaotic like that in much of Russia. During the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, Crimea changed hands numerous times and was for a time a stronghold of the anti-Bolshevik <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White Army</a>. The <a href="/wiki/White_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="White Army">White Army</a> controlled Crimea before remnants were finally driven out by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in November 1920. It was in Crimea that the White Russians led by <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Nikolayevich_Wrangel" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyotr Nikolayevich Wrangel">General Wrangel</a> made their last stand against <a href="/wiki/Nestor_Makhno" title="Nestor Makhno">Nestor Makhno</a> and the Red Army. When resistance was crushed, many of the anti-Communist fighters and civilians escaped by ship to <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. Between 56,000 and 150,000 of the Whites were murdered as part of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Terror" title="Red Terror">Red Terror</a>, organized by <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Kun" title="Béla Kun">Béla Kun</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Soviet_Union_.281921.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union_(1921–1991)">Soviet Union (1921–1991)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Oblast" title="Crimean Oblast">Crimean Oblast</a></div>
<p>Crimea became part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> in 1921 as the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, which became part of the Soviet Union in 1922.
</p>
<h4><span id="Autonomy_in_Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic_.281921.E2.80.931944.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomy_in_Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic_(1921–1944)">Autonomy in Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic (1921–1944)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jalta-confer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jalta-confer.jpg/220px-Jalta-confer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jalta-confer.jpg/330px-Jalta-confer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Jalta-confer.jpg/440px-Jalta-confer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="595" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jalta-confer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "<a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Big Three</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> in Crimea: <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Artek_(camp)" title="Artek (camp)">Artek youth camp</a> was created in 1925.
During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> the peninsula was <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Campaign">invaded</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanian_troops" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian troops">Romanian troops</a> in summer 1941 across the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">Isthmus of Perekop</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1941%E2%80%9342)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1941–42)">capture of Sevastopol</a> on 4 July 1942, Crimea was occupied until German and Romanian forces were expelled in an <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Offensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Offensive">offensive</a> by Soviet forces ending in May 1944. The Nazis <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Ukraine" title="The Holocaust in Ukraine">murdered</a> around 40,000 Crimean Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Region_in_Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic_.281945.E2.80.931954.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Region_in_Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic_(1945–1954)">Region in Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic (1945–1954)</span></h4>
<p>On 25 June 1946, it was downgraded to the Crimean Oblast, and the <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars were deported</a> for alleged collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> forces. A total of more than 230,000 people – about a fifth of the total population of the Crimean Peninsula at that time – were deported, mainly to <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>. 14,300 Greeks, 12,075 Bulgarians, and about 10,000 Armenians were also expelled.
</p>
<h4><span id="Region_in_Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_.281954.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Region_in_Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic_(1954–1991)">Region in Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic (1954–1991)</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">1954 transfer of Crimea</a></div>
<p>On 19 February 1954, the Presidium of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet" title="Supreme Soviet">Supreme Soviet</a> of the USSR issued <a href="/wiki/1954_transfer_of_Crimea" title="1954 transfer of Crimea">a decree on the transfer of the Crimean region of the RSFSR to the Ukrainian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This Supreme Soviet Decree states that this transfer was motivated by "the commonality of the economy, the proximity, and close economic and cultural relations between the Crimean region and the Ukrainian SSR".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> At that time no vote or referendum took place, and Crimean population had no say in the transfer (also typical of other Soviet border changes). After the annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation, doubts have been expressed - from the Russian side by all means, but even by Western historians (Richard Sakwa, "Frontline Ukraine. Crisis In the Borderlands", 2015) - about the very legitimacy of the 1954 transition of Crimea to Ukraine; in the critics' view the transition contradicted even the Soviet law.
</p><p>In post-war years, Crimea thrived as a <a href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourist destination">tourist destination</a>, with new attractions and sanatoriums for tourists. Tourists came from all around the Soviet Union and neighbouring countries, particularly from the <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="German Democratic Republic">German Democratic Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-blacksea-crimea/hist_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blacksea-crimea/hist-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In time the peninsula also became a major tourist destination for cruises originating in Greece and Turkey. Crimea's infrastructure and manufacturing also developed, particularly around the sea ports at <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> and in the oblast's landlocked capital, <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>. Populations of <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> alike doubled, with more than 1.6 million Russians and 626,000 Ukrainians living on the peninsula by 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-blacksea-crimea/hist_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blacksea-crimea/hist-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Ukrainian_Republic_.281991.E2.80.932014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukrainian_Republic_(1991–2014)">Ukrainian Republic (1991–2014)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg/220px-Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg/330px-Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg/440px-Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3141" data-file-height="2356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Simferopol_04-14_img18_K-Marx-Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>'s city centre</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/1991_Crimean_sovereignty_referendum" title="1991 Crimean sovereignty referendum">1991 Crimean sovereignty referendum</a></div>
<p>In January 1991, <a href="/wiki/1991_Crimean_sovereignty_referendum" title="1991 Crimean sovereignty referendum">a referendum was held</a> in the Crimean Oblast, and voters approved restoring the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Crimean Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a>. However, after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> less than a year later, the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> was formed as a constituent entity of independent Ukraine,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-szporluk_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szporluk-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> with a slight majority of Crimean voters approving Ukrainian independence in a December referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-doyle_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doyle-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 5 May 1992, the Crimean legislature declared conditional independence,<sup id="cite_ref-backind_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backind-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> but a referendum to confirm the decision was never held amid opposition from <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ukraine" title="Government of Ukraine">Kiev</a>: elected president of Crimea <a href="/wiki/Yuriy_Meshkov" title="Yuriy Meshkov">Yuriy Meshkov</a>, was replaced by Kiev appointed <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anatoliy_Franchuk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anatoliy Franchuk (page does not exist)">Anatoliy Franchuk</a>, which was done with the intent to rein in Crimean aspirations of autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-szporluk_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szporluk-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5_May_1992_in_Crimea_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5_May_1992_in_Crimea-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a>, the parliament of Crimea, voted to grant Crimea "extensive home rule" during the dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-doyle_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doyle-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-backind_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backind-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances" title="Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances">Budapest Memorandum on Security Assurances</a> acknowledged Ukrainian integrity.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_Crimean_parliamentary_election" title="2010 Crimean parliamentary election">last election</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada_of_Crimea" title="Verkhovna Rada of Crimea">Verkhovna Rada of Crimea</a> took place on 31 October 2010 and was won by the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Regions" title="Party of Regions">Party of Regions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 15 March 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Verkhovna Rada</a> of Ukraine officially dissolved the Verkhovna Rada of Crimea, and, on 17 March 2014, one day before the Russian annexation of Crimea,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_Crimea" title="State Council of Crimea">State Council of Crimea</a> was established in place of the Verkhovna Rada of Crimea.
</p>
<h3><span id="Russian_Federation_.28de_facto.2C_since_2014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Federation_(de_facto,_since_2014)">Russian Federation (de facto, since 2014)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a>; <a href="/wiki/Crimean_status_referendum,_2014" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean status referendum, 2014">Crimean status referendum, 2014</a>; <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">Political status of Crimea</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg/220px-2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg/330px-2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg/440px-2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2015._%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5_019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>June 2015: Tourists in Crimea with <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Russia" title="Flag of Russia">Russian flag</a> flying</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">2014 Ukrainian revolution</a> and the flight of Ukrainian President <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> on 21 February 2014, Russian President, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> stated to colleagues that "we must start working on returning Crimea to Russia."<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Within days, unmarked forces with local militias took over the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Autonomous Republic of Crimea">Autonomous Republic of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>, as well as occupying several localities in <a href="/wiki/Kherson_Oblast" title="Kherson Oblast">Kherson Oblast</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Arabat_Spit" title="Arabat Spit">Arabat Spit</a>, which is geographically a part of Crimea. Following a controversial referendum, the official results of which showed majority support for joining Russia, Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> signed a treaty of accession with the self-declared <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Crimea (country)">Republic of Crimea</a>, annexing it into the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian Federation</a> as two federal subjects: the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and the federal city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>. Though Russia had control over the peninsula, sovereignty <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea_and_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Political status of Crimea and Sevastopol">was disputed</a> as <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and the majority of the international community consider the annexation illegal,<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> as was shown by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> adopting a non-binding <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">resolution</a> calling upon states <i>not to recognise changes to the integrity of Ukraine</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> A range of <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">international sanctions</a> have remained in place against Russia and a number of named individuals as a result of the events of 2014.
</p><p>Russia withdrew its forces from southern Kherson in December 2014<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Since Russian control over Crimea was established in 2014, the peninsula has been administered as part of the Russian Federation except for the northern areas of the <a href="/wiki/Arabat_Spit" title="Arabat Spit">Arabat Spit</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Syvash" title="Syvash">Syvash</a> which are still controlled by Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within days of the signing of the accession treaty, the process of integrating Crimea into the Russian federation began: in March the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> went into official circulation<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and clocks were moved forward to Moscow time,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> in April a new revision of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Russian Constitution</a> was officially released with the Republic of Crimea and the federal city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> included in the list of <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal subjects of the Russian Federation">federal subjects of the Russian Federation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and in June the Russian ruble became the only form of legal tender.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In July 2015, Russian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> stated that Crimea had been fully integrated into Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B9_2019_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BC%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/May_Day" title="May Day">May Day</a> parade in <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>, in May 2019.</div></div></div>
<p>Since 2014 the Russian government has invested heavily in the peninsula's infrastructure—repairing roads, modernizing hospitals and building the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Bridge_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Bridge (Crimea)">Crimean Bridge</a> that links the peninsula to the Russian mainland. New sources of water are trying to be developed, with huge difficulties, to replace closed Ukrainian sources.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 the Russian government also began modernising the <a href="/wiki/Simferopol_International_Airport" title="Simferopol International Airport">Simferopol International Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> which opened its new terminal in April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russia provides electricity to Crimea via a cable beneath the Kerch Strait. In June 2018 there was a full electrical outage for all of Crimea, but the power grid company Rosseti reported to have fixed the outage in approximately one hour.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 December 2018, Russia completed a high-tech security fence marking the de facto border between Crimea and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h2>
<p>According to Article 10 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Constitution of the Republic of Crimea">Constitution of the Republic of Crimea</a>, there are three official languages in the republic: <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>. However, in practice, Russian is by far the main language.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The history of Crimea is complex as it lies at a conjunction of European and Asian peoples, with a mosaic of distinct and affiliated ethnic communities.  From the ancient period to the medieval period, the principal ethnic communities classed by linguistic origins are:
</p><p>-The Indo-European language family:
</p>
<dl><dd>-The Iranian language group comprising the Cimmerians, Scythians, Sarmatians, and the Alans</dd>
<dd>-The Greek language group comprising the Greeks, Byzantines, and the Spartocids (Hellenized)</dd>
<dd>-The Italic language group comprising the Romans, Venetians, and the Genoese</dd>
<dd>-The Germanic language group comprising the Goths, Ashkenazi Jews</dd>
<dd>-The Slavic language group comprising the Russians and Ukrainians</dd>
<dd>-The Armenian language group comprising the Armenians</dd></dl>
<p>-The Semitic language group comprising the Jews
</p><p>-The Turkic language family comprising the <a href="/wiki/Bulgar_language" title="Bulgar language">Bulgars</a>, Khazars, Kipchaks, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Tatars</a>, Turkicized Greeks (<a href="/wiki/Urums" title="Urums">Urums</a>), and the Ottomans
</p><p>-The Mongolic family is represented by the Mongols
</p><p>-The Huns were of uncertain linguistic origins.
</p><p>From the medieval period to the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> additional ethnic communities migrated to the area. Prominent representation includes the Armenian, German, Serbian, and Jewish ethnic communities.
</p>

class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Relief_map_of_Crimea_(disputed_status).jpg" title="File:Relief map of Crimea (disputed status).jpg"> </a></div>Geography of Crimea</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/East_European_Plain" title="East European Plain">East European Plain</a></div>
<p>Covering an area of 27,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (10,425&#160;sq&#160;mi), Crimea is located on the northern coast of the Black Sea and on the western coast of the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a>; the only land border is shared with Ukraine's <a href="/wiki/Kherson_Oblast" title="Kherson Oblast">Kherson Oblast</a> on the north. Crimea is almost an island and only connected to the continent by the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">Isthmus of Perekop</a>, a strip of land about 5–7 kilometres (3.1–4.3&#160;mi) wide.
</p><p>Much of the natural border between the Crimean Peninsula and the Ukrainian mainland comprises the <a href="/wiki/Sivash" class="mw-redirect" title="Sivash">Sivash</a> or "Rotten Sea", a large system of shallow lagoons stretching along the western shore of the Sea of Azov. Besides the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">isthmus of Perekop</a>, the peninsula is connected to the Kherson Oblast's <a href="/wiki/Henichesk_Raion" title="Henichesk Raion">Henichesk Raion</a> by bridges over the narrow Chonhar and Henichesk straits and over Kerch Strait to the <a href="/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai" title="Krasnodar Krai">Krasnodar Krai</a>. The northern part of <a href="/wiki/Arabat_Spit" title="Arabat Spit">Arabat Spit</a> is administratively part of Henichesk Raion in Kherson Oblast, including its two rural communities of <a href="/wiki/Shchaslyvtseve" title="Shchaslyvtseve">Shchaslyvtseve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strilkove" title="Strilkove">Strilkove</a>. The eastern tip of the Crimean peninsula comprises the <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Peninsula" title="Kerch Peninsula">Kerch Peninsula</a>, separated from <a href="/wiki/Taman_Peninsula" title="Taman Peninsula">Taman Peninsula</a> on the Russian mainland by the <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Strait" title="Kerch Strait">Kerch Strait</a>, which connects the Black Sea with the Sea of Azov, at a width of between 3–13 kilometres (1.9–8.1&#160;mi).
</p><p>Geographers generally divide the peninsula into three zones: <a href="/wiki/Pontic_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontic steppe">steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean coast">southern coast</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places">Places</span></h3>
