style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left">Simferopol</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:59.524%;left:50%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Karasu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Karasu" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;bottom:5px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px">Karasu</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:60.476%;left:61.136%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Stary Krym" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Stary Krym" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;bottom:5px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px">Stary<br />Krym</div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:28.095%;left:45.227%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Dzhankoy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Dzhankoy" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:5px;left:-3em;text-align:center"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px">Dzhankoy</div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Relief_map_of_Crimea_(disputed_status).jpg" title="File:Relief map of Crimea (disputed status).jpg"> </a></div>Places in Crimea</div></div></div>
<p>Given its long history and many conquerors, most towns in Crimea have several names.
</p><p><b>West:</b> The <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Perekop" title="Isthmus of Perekop">Isthmus of Perekop</a> /<a href="/wiki/Perekop" title="Perekop">Perekop</a>/<a href="/wiki/Or_Qapi" title="Or Qapi">Or Qapi</a>, about 7&#160;km wide, connects Crimea to the mainland. It was often fortified and sometimes garrisoned by the Turks. The <a href="/wiki/North_Crimean_Canal" title="North Crimean Canal">North Crimean Canal</a> now crosses it to bring water from the Dnieper. To the west <a href="/wiki/Karkinit_Bay" title="Karkinit Bay">Karkinit Bay</a> separates the <a href="/wiki/Tarkhankut_Peninsula" title="Tarkhankut Peninsula">Tarkhankut Peninsula</a> from the mainland. On the north side of the peninsula is <a href="/wiki/Chernomorskoe" class="mw-redirect" title="Chernomorskoe">Chernomorskoe</a>/Kalos <a href="/wiki/Liman_(landform)" title="Liman (landform)">Limen</a>. On the south side is the large <a href="/wiki/Donuzlav" title="Donuzlav">Donuzlav</a> Bay and the port and ancient Greek settlement of Eupatoria/<a href="/wiki/Yevpatoria" title="Yevpatoria">Yevpatoria</a>/Kerkinitis/Gozleve. The coast then runs south to <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>/<a href="/wiki/Chersonesus" title="Chersonesus">Chersonesus</a>, a good natural harbor, great naval base and the largest city on the peninsula. At the head of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol_Bay" title="Sevastopol Bay">Sevastopol Bay</a> stands <a href="/wiki/Inkermann" class="mw-redirect" title="Inkermann">Inkermann</a>/Kalamita. South of Sevastopol is the small <a href="/wiki/Heracles_Peninsula" title="Heracles Peninsula">Heracles Peninsula</a>.
</p><p><b>South:</b> In the south, between the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a> and the sea runs a narrow coastal strip which was <a href="/wiki/Gazaria_(Genoese_colonies)" title="Gazaria (Genoese colonies)">held by the Genoese</a> and (after 1475) by the Turks. Under Russian rule it became a kind of <a href="/wiki/Riviera" title="Riviera">riviera</a>. In Soviet times the many palaces were replaced<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2019)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> with <a href="/wiki/Dacha" title="Dacha">dachas</a> and health resorts. From west to east are: <a href="/wiki/Heracles_Peninsula" title="Heracles Peninsula">Heracles Peninsula</a>; <a href="/wiki/Balaklava" title="Balaklava">Balaklava</a>/Symbalon/Cembalo, a smaller natural harbor south of Sevastopol; <a href="/wiki/Foros,_Crimea" title="Foros, Crimea">Foros</a>, the southernmost point; <a href="/wiki/Alupka" title="Alupka">Alupka</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Vorontsov_Palace_(Alupka)" title="Vorontsov Palace (Alupka)">Vorontsov Palace (Alupka)</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gaspra" title="Gaspra">Gaspra</a>; <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">Yalta</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gurzuf" title="Gurzuf">Gurzuf</a>; <a href="/wiki/Alushta" title="Alushta">Alushta</a>. Further east is <a href="/wiki/Sudak" title="Sudak">Sudak</a>/Sougdia/Soldaia with its Genoese fort. Further east still is Kaffa/Theodosia/<a href="/wiki/Feodosia" title="Feodosia">Feodosia</a>, once a great <a href="/wiki/Slave_market" title="Slave market">slave-mart</a> and a kind of capital for the Genoese and Turks. Unlike the other southern ports, Feodosia has no mountains to its north. At the east end of the 90&#160;km <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Peninsula" title="Kerch Peninsula">Kerch Peninsula</a> is <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a>/<a href="/wiki/Panticapaeum" title="Panticapaeum">Panticapaeum</a>, once the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Bosporian_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosporian Kingdom">Bosporian Kingdom</a>. Just south of Kerch the new <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Bridge" title="Crimean Bridge">Crimean Bridge</a> (opened in 2018) connects Crimea to the <a href="/wiki/Taman_Peninsula" title="Taman Peninsula">Taman Peninsula</a>.
</p><p><b>Sea of Azov:</b> There is little on the south shore. The west shore is marked by the <a href="/wiki/Arabat_Spit" title="Arabat Spit">Arabat Spit</a>. Behind it is the <a href="/wiki/Syvash" title="Syvash">Syvash</a> or "Putrid Sea", a system of lakes and marshes which in the far north extend west to the Perekop Isthmus. Road- and rail-bridges cross the northern part of Syvash.
</p><p><b>Interior:</b> Most of the former capitals of Crimea stood on the north side of the mountains. <a href="/wiki/Mangup" title="Mangup">Mangup</a>/Doros (Gothic, Theodoro). <a href="/wiki/Bakhchisarai" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakhchisarai">Bakhchisarai</a> (1532-1783).
Southeast of Bakhchisarai is the cliff-fort of <a href="/wiki/Chufut-Kale" title="Chufut-Kale">Chufut-Kale</a>/Qirq Or which was used in more warlike times. <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>/Ak-Mechet, the modern capital. <a href="/wiki/Karasu-Bazar" class="mw-redirect" title="Karasu-Bazar">Karasu-Bazar</a>/Bilohorsk was a commercial center. Solkhat/<a href="/wiki/Stary_Krym" title="Stary Krym">Stary Krym</a> was the old Tatar capital. Towns on the northern steppe area are all modern, notably <a href="/wiki/Dzhankoy" title="Dzhankoy">Dzhankoy</a>, a major road- and rail-junction.
</p><p><b>Rivers:</b> The longest is the <a href="/wiki/Salhir_River" title="Salhir River">Salhir River</a> which rises southeast of Simferopol and flows north and northeast to the Sea of Azov. The <a href="/wiki/Alma_River_(Crimea)" title="Alma River (Crimea)">Alma River</a> flows west to reach the Black Sea between Eupatoria and Sevastopol. The shorter <a href="/wiki/Chornaya_River_(Crimea)" title="Chornaya River (Crimea)">Chornaya River (Crimea)</a> flows west to Sevastopol Bay.
</p><p><b>Nearby:</b> East of the Kerch Strait the Ancient Greeks founded colonies at <a href="/wiki/Phanagoria" title="Phanagoria">Phanagoria</a> (at the head of <a href="/wiki/Taman_Bay" title="Taman Bay">Taman Bay</a>), <a href="/wiki/Hermonassa" class="mw-redirect" title="Hermonassa">Hermonassa</a> (later Tmutarakan and <a href="/wiki/Taman,_Russia" title="Taman, Russia">Taman</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gorgippia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorgippia">Gorgippia</a> (later a Turkish port and now Anapa). At the northeast point of the Sea of Azov at the mouth of the Don River were <a href="/wiki/Tanais" title="Tanais">Tanais</a>, Azak/<a href="/wiki/Azov" title="Azov">Azov</a> and now <a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">Rostov-on-Don</a>. North of the peninsula the Dnieper turns westward and enters the Black Sea through the east-west <a href="/wiki/Dnieper-Bug_Estuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper-Bug Estuary">Dnieper-Bug Estuary</a> which also receives the Bug River. At the mouth of the Bug stood <a href="/wiki/Olvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Olvia">Olvia</a>. At the mouth of the estuary is <a href="/wiki/Ochakiv" title="Ochakiv">Ochakiv</a>. <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> stands where the coast turns southwest. Further southwest is <a href="/wiki/Tyras" title="Tyras">Tyras</a>/Akkerman/<a href="/wiki/Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi" title="Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi">Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg/220px-Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg/330px-Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg/440px-Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2948" data-file-height="1912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kanaka._Crimea._Urraine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>South coast of Crimea</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_Mountains">Crimean Mountains</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg/220px-Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg/330px-Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg/440px-Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1468" data-file-height="1056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eklizi-Burun-mountain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eclizee-Burun Mountain</div></div></div>
<p>The southeast coast is flanked at a distance of 8–12 kilometres (5.0–7.5&#160;mi) from the sea by a parallel range of mountains: the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> These mountains are backed by <a href="/wiki/Cuesta" title="Cuesta">secondary parallel ranges</a>.
</p><p>The main range of these mountains rises with extraordinary abruptness from the deep floor of the Black Sea to an altitude of 600–1,545 metres (1,969–5,069&#160;ft), beginning at the southwest point of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a>, called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Fiolente&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cape Fiolente (page does not exist)">Cape Fiolente</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A4%D1%96%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82" class="extiw" title="uk:Фіолент">uk</a>&#93;</span>.  It was believed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2019)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that this cape was supposedly crowned with the temple of <a href="/wiki/Artemis" title="Artemis">Artemis</a> where <a href="/wiki/Iphigeneia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iphigeneia">Iphigeneia</a> is said to have officiated as priestess.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Uchan-su_(waterfall)" title="Uchan-su (waterfall)">Uchan-su</a>, on the south slope of the mountains, is the highest waterfall in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span></h3>
<p>There are 257 rivers and major streams on the Crimean peninsula; they are primarily fed by rainwater, with snowmelt playing a very minor role. This makes for significant annual fluctuation in water flow, with many streams drying up completely during the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The largest rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Salhir_River" title="Salhir River">Salhir</a> (Salğır, Салгир), the Kacha (Кача), the <a href="/wiki/Alma_River_(Crimea)" title="Alma River (Crimea)">Alma</a> (Альма), and the Belbek (Бельбек).  Also important are the Kokozka (Kökköz or Коккозка), the Indole (Indol or Индо́л), the <a href="/wiki/Chornaya_River_(Crimea)" title="Chornaya River (Crimea)">Chorna</a> (Çorğun, Chernaya or Чёрная), the Derekoika (Dereköy or Дерекойка),<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> the Karasu-Bashi (Biyuk-Karasu or Биюк-Карасу) (tributary of Salhir river), the Burulcha (Бурульча) (tributary of Salhir river), the <a href="/wiki/Uchan-su_(river)" title="Uchan-su (river)">Uchan-su</a>, and the Ulu-Uzen'. The longest river of Crimea is the Salhir at 204&#160;km. The Belbek has the greatest average discharge at 2.16 cubic metres per second (76&#160;cu&#160;ft/s).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The Alma and the Kacha are the second- and third-longest rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-BSE_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSE-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are more than fifty salt lakes and <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt pans</a> on the peninsula, the largest of them is Lake Sasyk (Сасык) on the southwest coast; others include <a href="/wiki/Aqtas_Lake" title="Aqtas Lake">Aqtas</a>, Koyashskoye, Kiyatskoe, Kirleutskoe, Kizil-Yar, Bakalskoe, and <a href="/wiki/Donuzlav" title="Donuzlav">Donuzlav</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The general trend is for the former lakes to become salt pans.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Syvash" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Syvash">Lake Syvash</a> (Sıvaş or Сива́ш) is a system of interconnected shallow <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoons</a> on the north-eastern coast, covering an area of around 2,560&#160;km2. A number of dams have created reservoirs, among the largest are the Simferopolskoye, Alminskoye,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> the Taygansky and the Belogorsky just south of <a href="/wiki/Bilohirsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilohirsk">Bilohirsk</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bilohirsk_Raion" title="Bilohirsk Raion">Bilohirsk Raion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Crimean_Canal" title="North Crimean Canal">North Crimea Canal</a>, which transports water from the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a>, is the largest of the man-made irrigation channels on the peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-construction_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Steppe">Steppe</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pontic-Caspian_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontic-Caspian steppe">Pontic-Caspian steppe</a></div>
<p>Seventy-five percent of the remaining area of Crimea consists of semiarid <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairie</a> lands, a southward continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Pontic-Caspian_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontic-Caspian steppe">Pontic-Caspian steppe</a>, which slope gently to the northwest from the foothills of the Crimean Mountains.
Numerous <a href="/wiki/Kurgan" title="Kurgan">kurgans</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Burial_mound" class="mw-redirect" title="Burial mound">burial mounds</a>, of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythians</a> are scattered across the Crimean steppes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimean_Riviera">Crimean Riviera</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%AF%D0%BB%D1%82%D0%B0_%D0%AE%D0%B6%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B3_%D0%94%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">Crimean Mountains</a> in the background and <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">Yalta</a> as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Tsar%27s_Path" title="Tsar&#39;s Path">Tsar's Path</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The terrain that lies south of the sheltering Crimean Mountain range is of an altogether different character. Here, the narrow strip of coast and the slopes of the mountains are smothered with greenery. This "riviera" stretches along the southeast coast from capes <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Fiolente&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cape Fiolente (page does not exist)">Fiolente</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Aya" title="Cape Aya">Aya</a>, in the south, to Feodosiya. It is studded with summer sea-bathing resorts such as <a href="/wiki/Alupka" title="Alupka">Alupka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">Yalta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurzuf" title="Gurzuf">Gurzuf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alushta" title="Alushta">Alushta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudak" title="Sudak">Sudak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Feodosiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Feodosiya">Feodosiya</a>. During the years of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> rule, the resorts and <a href="/wiki/Dacha" title="Dacha">dachas</a> of this coast served as prime perquisites of the politically loyal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup>why here? and ref?</sup> In addition, vineyards and fruit orchards are located in the region. Fishing, mining, and the production of <a href="/wiki/Essential_oil" title="Essential oil">essential oils</a> are also important. Numerous Crimean Tatar villages, mosques, <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">monasteries</a>, and palaces of the Russian imperial family and nobles are found here, as well as picturesque ancient Greek and medieval castles.
</p><p>The Crimean Mountains and the southern coast are part of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Submediterranean_forest_complex" title="Crimean Submediterranean forest complex">Crimean Submediterranean forest complex</a> ecoregion. The natural vegetation consists of scrublands, woodlands, and forests, with a climate and vegetation similar to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg/220px-Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg/330px-Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg/440px-Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2589" data-file-height="1725" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Novyi_Svit_IMG_2941_1725.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Crimea's south coast has a subtropical climate</div></div></div>
<p>Crimea is located between the <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a> belts and is characterized by warm and sunny weather.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> It is characterized by diversity and the presence of microclimates.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The northern parts of Crimea have a moderate <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> with short, mild winters and moderately hot dry summers.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In the central and mountainous areas the climate is transitional between the continental climate to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Winters are mild at lower altitudes (in the foothills) and colder at higher altitudes.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Summers are hot at lower altitudes and warm in the mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> A subtropical, Mediterranean climate dominates the southern coastal regions, is characterized by mild winters and moderately hot, dry summers.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The climate of Crimea is influenced by its geographic location, relief, and influences from the <a href="/wiki/Black_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Black sea">Black sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Crimean coast is shielded from cold air masses coming from the north and, as a result, has milder winters.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Maritime influences from the Black Sea are restricted to coastal areas; in the interior of the peninsula the maritime influence is weak and does not play an important role.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Because a high-pressure system is located north of Crimea in both summer and winter, winds predominantly come from the north and northeast year-round.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In winter these winds bring in cold, dry continental air, while in summer they bring in dry and hot weather.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Winds from the northwest bring warm and wet air from the Atlantic Ocean, causing precipitation during spring and summer.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> As well, winds from the southwest bring very warm and wet air from the subtropical latitudes of the Atlantic Ocean and the Mediterranean sea and cause precipitation during fall and winter.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mean annual temperatures range from 10&#160;°C (50.0&#160;°F) in the far north (<a href="/wiki/Armiansk" class="mw-redirect" title="Armiansk">Armiansk</a>) to 13&#160;°C (55.4&#160;°F) in the far south (<a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">Yalta</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In the mountains, the mean annual temperature is around 5.7&#160;°C (42.3&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> For every 100&#160;m (330&#160;ft) increase in altitude, temperatures decrease by 0.65&#160;°C (1.17&#160;°F) while precipitation increases.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In January mean temperatures range from −3&#160;°C (26.6&#160;°F) in Armiansk to 4.4&#160;°C (39.9&#160;°F) in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Myskhor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Myskhor (page does not exist)">Myskhor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Cool-season temperatures average around 7&#160;°C (44.6&#160;°F) and it is rare for the weather to drop below freezing except in the mountains, where there is usually snow.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In July mean temperatures range from 15.4&#160;°C (59.7&#160;°F) in <a href="/wiki/Ai-Petri" title="Ai-Petri">Ai-Petri</a> to 23.4&#160;°C (74.1&#160;°F) in the central parts of Crimea to 24.4&#160;°C (75.9&#160;°F) in Myskhor.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The frost-free period ranges from 160–200 days in the steppe and mountain regions to 240–260 days on the south coast.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Precipitation in Crimea varies significantly based on location; it ranges from 310 millimetres (12.2&#160;in) in <a href="/wiki/Chornomorske" title="Chornomorske">Chornomorske</a> to 1,220 millimetres (48.0&#160;in) at the highest altitudes in the Crimean mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Crimean mountains greatly influence the amount of precipitation present in the peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> However, most of Crimea (88.5%) receives 300 to 500 millimetres (11.8 to 19.7&#160;in) of precipitation per year.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The plains usually receive 300 to 400 millimetres (11.8 to 15.7&#160;in) of precipitation per year, increasing to 560 millimetres (22.0&#160;in) in the southern coast at sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The western parts of the Crimean mountains receive more than 1,000 millimetres (39.4&#160;in) of precipitation per year.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Snowfall is common in the mountains during winter.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeageography_83-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeageography-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Most of the peninsula receives more than 2,000 sunshine hours per year; it reaches up to 2,505 sunshine hours in Karabi–Yayla in the Crimean mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the climate favors recreation and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-crimeaclimate_82-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimeaclimate-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Because of its climate and subsidized travel-packages from Russian state-run companies, the southern Crimean coast has remained a popular resort for Russian tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategic_value">Strategic value</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Varangian_routes.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Varangian_routes.png/220px-Varangian_routes.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Varangian_routes.png/330px-Varangian_routes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Varangian_routes.png/440px-Varangian_routes.png 2x" data-file-width="872" data-file-height="605" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Varangian_routes.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Trade_route_from_the_Varangians_to_the_Greeks" title="Trade route from the Varangians to the Greeks">historical trade route</a> (shown in purple) connecting <a href="/wiki/Uppsala" title="Uppsala">Uppsala</a> with <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> via <a href="/wiki/Chersonesus_(Crimea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chersonesus (Crimea)">Cherson</a>. The major centers of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Kievan Rus'</a> - <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> itself, <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Staraya_Ladoga" title="Staraya Ladoga">Ladoga</a> - arose along this route.</div></div></div><p> The Black Sea ports of Crimea provide quick access to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and Middle East. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Crimea" title="History of Crimea">Historically</a>, possession of the southern coast of Crimea was sought after by most empires of the greater region since antiquity (<a href="/wiki/Roman_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Crimea">Roman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherson_(theme)" title="Cherson (theme)">Byzantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gedik_Ahmed_Pasha" title="Gedik Ahmed Pasha">Ottoman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">British and French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1941%E2%80%9342)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1941–42)">Nazi German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet#Soviet_Navy" title="Black Sea Fleet">Soviet</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The nearby <a href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper River</a> is a major waterway and transportation route that crosses the European continent from north to south and ultimately links the Black Sea with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, of strategic importance since the historical <a href="/wiki/Trade_route_from_the_Varangians_to_the_Greeks" title="Trade route from the Varangians to the Greeks">trade route from the Varangians to the Greeks</a>. The Black Sea serves as an economic thoroughfare connecting the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> region and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Crimea_Annexation_&#39;Robbery_on_International_Scale&#39;_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crimea_Annexation_&#39;Robbery_on_International_Scale&#39;-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Transport_Workers%27_Federation" title="International Transport Workers&#39; Federation">International Transport Workers' Federation</a>, as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Crimea&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there were at least 12 operating merchant seaports in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-Черное_море_признано_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Черное_море_признано-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg/220px-Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg/330px-Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg/440px-Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="2992" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koreiz_-_beach3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tourism is an important sector of Crimea's economy</div></div></div>
<p>In 2016 Crimea had Nominal GDP of <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>7 billion and <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a>3,000 per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main branches of the modern Crimean economy are agriculture and fishing oysters pearls, industry and manufacturing, tourism, and ports. Industrial plants are situated for the most part in the southern coast (Eupatoria Sevastopol Feodosia Kerch) regions of the republic, few northern (Armyansk Krasnoperekopsk Dzhankoj), aside from the central area, mainly Simferopol okrug and eastern region in Nizhnegorsk (few plants, same for Dzhankoj) city. Important industrial cities include <a href="/wiki/Dzhankoy" title="Dzhankoy">Dzhankoy</a>, housing a major railway connection, <a href="/wiki/Krasnoperekopsk" title="Krasnoperekopsk">Krasnoperekopsk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armyansk" title="Armyansk">Armyansk</a>, among others.
</p><p>After the Russian annexation of Crimea in early 2014 and subsequent sanctions targeting Crimea, the tourist industry suffered major losses for two years. The flow of holidaymakers dropped 35 percent in the first half of 2014 over the same period of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The number of tourist arrivals reached a record in 2012 at 6.1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> According to the Russian administration of Crimea, they dropped to 3.8 million in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and rebounded to 5.6 million by 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most important industries in Crimea include food production, chemical fields, mechanical engineering, and metalworking, and fuel production industries.<sup id="cite_ref-CMU_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Sixty percent of the industry market belongs to food production. There are a total of 291 large industrial enterprises and 1002 small business enterprises.<sup id="cite_ref-CMU_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agriculture in the region includes cereals, vegetable-growing, gardening, and <a href="/wiki/Winemaking_in_Crimea" title="Winemaking in Crimea">wine-making</a>, particularly in the Yalta and <a href="/wiki/Massandra" title="Massandra">Massandra</a> regions. Livestock production includes cattle breeding, poultry keeping, and sheep breeding.<sup id="cite_ref-CMU_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Other products produced on the Crimean Peninsula include salt, <a href="/wiki/Porphyry_(geology)" title="Porphyry (geology)">porphyry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ironstone" title="Ironstone">ironstone</a> (found around <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a>) since ancient times.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the republic's annual GDP was $4.3 billion (500 times smaller than the size of Russia's economy). The average salary was $290 per month. The <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_balance" title="Government budget balance">budget deficit</a> was $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<p>Crimea also possesses several <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas field">natural gas fields</a> both <a href="/wiki/Onshore_(hydrocarbons)" title="Onshore (hydrocarbons)">onshore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Offshore_(hydrocarbons)" title="Offshore (hydrocarbons)">offshore</a>, which were starting to be drilled by western oil and gas companies before annexation.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The inland fields are located in <a href="/wiki/Chornomorske_Raion" title="Chornomorske Raion">Chornomorske</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dzhankoy_municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzhankoy municipality">Dzhankoy</a>, while offshore fields are located in the western coast in the Black Sea and in the northeastern coast in the Azov Sea:<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The republic also possesses two <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil field">oil fields</a>: one onshore, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Serebryankse_oil_field&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Serebryankse oil field (page does not exist)">Serebryankse oil field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rozdolne_Raion" title="Rozdolne Raion">Rozdolne</a>, and one offshore, the <a href="/wiki/Subbotina_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Subbotina oil field">Subbotina oil field</a> in the Black Sea.
</p>
<dl><dt>Electricity</dt></dl>
<p>Crimea has 540 MW of its own electricity generation capacity including Simferopol Thermal Power Plant (100 MW), Sevastopol Thermal Power Plant (22 MW) and Kamish-Burunskaya Thermal Power Plant (19 MW).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  This is insufficient for local consumption and since annexation by Russia, Crimea is reliant on an underwater power cable to mainland Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Building and near start up are two combined cycle gas steam turbo thermal plants PGU, both 470 MW (116 167 MW GT, 235 MW block), build (plant) by TPE along others and turbines by Power Machines (UTZ KalugaTZ&#160;?), NPO Saturn with Perm PMZ, either GTD-110M modified or GTE-160 or 180 units or UTZ KTZ or a V94.2 bought by MAPNA, modified in Russian plants for PGU Thermal plants specifics. Also many solar photovoltaic SES plants lie along the peninsula (north of Sevastopol too, a smaller facility). Also gas thermal Saki plant close to Jodobrom chemical plant and SaKhZ(SaChP) boosted production with Perm GTE GTU25P (PS90GP25 25 MW aeroderivative GP) PGU turbogenerators. Older plants are Sevastopol TEC (close to Inkerman) which use AEG and Ganz Elektro turbines and turbogenerators about 25 MW each, Sinferopol TEC (north, in Agrarne locale) Eupatoria, Kamysh Burun TEC (Kerch south - Zaliv) and few others.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3>
<table class="box-Lacking_overview plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>contains an enumeration of examples, but lacks a general overview of its topic.</b> You can help by adding an appropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style_(lists)#Lead_paragraphs_in_embedded_lists" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style (lists)">introductory section</a>. <a href="/wiki/Help:Editing" title="Help:Editing">Editing help</a> is available. <small><i>(March 2014)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<dl><dt>Crimean Bridge</dt></dl>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_(2018-05-15)_16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg/220px-Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg/330px-Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg/440px-Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_%282018-05-15%29_16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_Crimean_bridge_(2018-05-15)_16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Crimean_Bridge" title="Crimean Bridge">Crimean Bridge</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg/170px-Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg/255px-Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg/340px-Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3152" data-file-height="3152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crimea_South_Coast_04-14_img01_Simferopol-Yalta_trolley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trolleybus near Alushta</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Kanatka.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Yalta_Kanatka.JPG/220px-Yalta_Kanatka.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Yalta_Kanatka.JPG/330px-Yalta_Kanatka.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Yalta_Kanatka.JPG/440px-Yalta_Kanatka.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Kanatka.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cableway in Yalta</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Bridge" title="Crimean Bridge">Crimean Bridge</a></div>
<p>In May 2015, work began on a multibillion-dollar road-rail link (a pair of parallel bridges) across the Kerch Strait.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The road bridge opened in May 2018, and the rail bridge is projected to be fully completed and operational by 2019. With a length of 19&#160;km, it is the longest bridge in Europe, as it overcame <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Bridge" title="Vasco da Gama Bridge">Vasco da Gama Bridge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Public transportation</dt></dl>
<p>Almost every settlement in Crimea is connected with another settlement by bus lines. Crimea contains the longest (96&#160;km or 59&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Trolleybus" title="Crimean Trolleybus">trolleybus route</a> in the world, stretching from Simferopol to Yalta.<sup id="cite_ref-Crimea_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crimea-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The trolleybus line starts near <a href="/wiki/Simferopol" title="Simferopol">Simferopol</a>'s Railway Station (in Soviet times it started near <a href="/wiki/Simferopol_International_Airport" title="Simferopol International Airport">Simferopol International Airport</a>) through the mountains to <a href="/wiki/Alushta" title="Alushta">Alushta</a> and on to Yalta. The length of line is about 90&#160;km and passengers are assigned a seat. It was founded in 1959.
</p><p>Railroad lines running through Crimea include <a href="/wiki/Armyansk" title="Armyansk">Armyansk</a>—Kerch (with a link to Feodosiya), and <a href="/wiki/Melitopol" title="Melitopol">Melitopol</a>—Sevastopol (with a link to Yevpatoria), connecting Crimea to the Ukrainian mainland.
</p>
<dl><dt>International airport</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Simferopol_International_Airport" title="Simferopol International Airport">Simferopol International Airport</a>'s new terminal opened in from April 2018 with the ability to handle 6.5 million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> It was built in 22 months and covers an area of 78,000 square meters.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<dl><dt>Highways</dt></dl>
<ul><li>(under construction) Tavrida highway (route (Eupatoria-)Sevastopol - Simferopol (SW to W N to East ring) - Belogorsk <br /> - north Feodosia - Kerch south (strait bridge) .</li>

<dl><dt>Railways</dt></dl>
<ul><li>Armyansk Dzhankoi, Dzhankoi Sinferopol, Eupatoria Sinferopol</li>
<li>Sevastopol Sinferopol, Dzhankoi Nezhgorsk (Feodosia) Kerch, Kerch (bridge) Taman Krasnodar</li>
<li>project building shortcut north Simferopol south Nezhgorsk or Sinferopol Belogorsk (Feodosia) Kerch route</li></ul>
<dl><dt>Sea transport</dt></dl>
<p>The cities of Yalta, <a href="/wiki/Feodosiya" class="mw-redirect" title="Feodosiya">Feodosiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a>, Sevastopol, Chornomorske and <a href="/wiki/Yevpatoria" title="Yevpatoria">Yevpatoria</a> are connected to one another by sea routes. In the cities of Yevpatoria and nearby <a href="/wiki/Urban-type_settlement" title="Urban-type settlement">townlet</a> Molochnoye are tram systems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_(3943047709).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg/220px-Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg/330px-Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg/440px-Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_%283943047709%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boardwalk_at_Yalta_Ukraine_(3943047709).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boardwalk in Yalta.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg/220px-THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg/330px-THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg/440px-THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2992" data-file-height="1969" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_GENOESE_FORTRESS_IN_CAFFA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> fortress of <a href="/wiki/Feodosia" title="Feodosia">Caffa</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg/220px-Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg/330px-Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg/440px-Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="3333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baht%C5%A1isarai-Khaani_palee_Krimmis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mosque and yard in the Khan Palace in <a href="/wiki/Bakhchisaray" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakhchisaray">Bakhchisaray</a></div></div></div>
<p>The development of Crimea as a holiday destination began in the second half of the 19th century. The development of the transport networks brought masses of tourists from central parts of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.
At the beginning of the 20th century, a major development of palaces, villas, and dachas began—most of which remain. These are some of the main attractions of Crimea as a tourist destination. There are many <a href="/wiki/Crimean_legends" title="Crimean legends">Crimean legends</a> about famous touristic places, which attract the attention of tourists.
</p><p>A new phase of tourist development began when the Soviet government realised the potential of the healing quality of the local air, lakes and therapeutic muds. It became a "health" destination for Soviet workers, and hundreds of thousands of Soviet tourists visited Crimea.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Artek_(camp)" title="Artek (camp)">Artek</a> is a former <a href="/wiki/Young_Pioneer_camp" title="Young Pioneer camp">Young Pioneer camp</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> in the town of <a href="/wiki/Hurzuf" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurzuf">Hurzuf</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Ayu-Dag" title="Ayu-Dag">Ayu-Dag</a>, established in 1925.  In 1969 it had an area of 3.2&#160;km². The camp consisted of 150 buildings Unlike most of the young pioneer camps, Artek was an all-year camp, due to the warm climate. Artek was considered to be a privilege for Soviet children during its existence, as well as for children from other communist countries. During its heyday, 27,000 children a year vacationed at Artek. Between 1925 and 1969 the camp hosted 300,000 children.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> After the breaking up of the <a href="/wiki/Young_Pioneer_organization_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Pioneer organization of the Soviet Union">Young Pioneers</a> in 1991 its prestige declined, though it remained a popular vacation destination.<sup id="cite_ref-tub_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tub-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1990s, Crimea became more of a get-away destination than a "health-improvement" destination. The most visited areas are the south shore of Crimea with cities of Yalta and Alushta, the western shore – Eupatoria and Saki, and the south-eastern shore – Feodosia and Sudak.
According to <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic</a>, Crimea was among the top 20 travel destinations in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Places of interest include
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions">Sanctions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis</a></div>
<p>Following Russia's largely unrecognized annexation of Crimea, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the United States, Canada, Australia, Japan, and several other countries (including Ukraine) imposed <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">economic sanctions</a> against Russia, including some specifically targeting Crimea.  Many of these sanctions were directed at individuals—both Russian and Crimean.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In general they prohibit the sale, supply, transfer, or export of <a href="/wiki/Good_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Good (economics)">goods</a> and technology in several sectors, including services directly related to tourism and infrastructure. They list seven ports where <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a> cannot dock.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Sanctions against individuals include travel bans and asset freezes. <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> and <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> temporarily stopped service in Crimea in December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The Russian national payment card system now allows Visa and MasterCard cards issued by Russian banks to work in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-RT.com_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT.com-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mir_(payment_system)" title="Mir (payment system)">Mir payment system</a> operated by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Russia" title="Central Bank of Russia">Central Bank of Russia</a> operates in Crimea as well as Master Card and Visa.<sup id="cite_ref-RT.com_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT.com-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> However, there are no major international banks in the Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Crimea" title="Politics of Crimea">Politics of Crimea</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">Federal subjects of Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg/220px-Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg/330px-Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg/440px-Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Concert_%C2%ABCrimean_spring._Five_years_in_his_native_Harbor%C2%BB_40.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Concert to mark the fifth anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Annexation" title="Annexation">annexation</a> in Sevastopol, Crimea, March 2019</div></div></div>
<p>The politics of Crimea is that of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> on one hand, and that of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> on the other. Since becoming the 84th and 85th Federal Subjects of the Russian Federation in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> both have strongly supported <a href="/wiki/United_Russia" title="United Russia">United Russia</a> in both local and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Russia" title="Elections in Russia">national elections</a>.
</p><p>At the most recent <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_parliamentary_election" title="2014 Crimean parliamentary election">Crimean parliamentary election on 14 September 2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Russia" title="United Russia">United Russia</a> won 70 of the 75 seats in the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_Crimea" title="State Council of Crimea">State Council of Crimea</a> based on just over 70% of the vote. Despite calls from local <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> for a boycott of the elections, turnout was over 53% which compared well with elections in other regions of Russia. Following the election, <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Aksyonov" title="Sergey Aksyonov">Sergey Aksyonov</a> became <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea" title="Head of the Republic of Crimea">Head of the Republic of Crimea</a>: he had previously been Acting Head from 14 April 2014. United Russia is also the leading party in the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Sevastopol" title="Legislative Assembly of Sevastopol">Legislative Assembly of Sevastopol</a> having won 22 of the 24 seats at the last election.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Sevastopol_(Russia)" title="Governor of Sevastopol (Russia)">Governor of Sevastopol</a> is <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Ovsyannikov" title="Dmitry Ovsyannikov">Dmitry Ovsyannikov</a> who was first appointed on 28 July 2016 following the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Menyaylo" title="Sergey Menyaylo">Sergey Menyaylo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2017_Sevastopol_gubernatorial_election" title="2017 Sevastopol gubernatorial election">secured re-election</a> on 71% of the vote on 10 September 2017.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/United_Russia" title="United Russia">United Russia</a> maintained its position as the most supported political party across Crimea at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Russian_legislative_election" title="2016 Russian legislative election">Russian legislative election on 18 September 2016</a>, achieving 72.8% of the vote.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://ria.ru/infografika/20160918/1476912507.html#/summary">[2]</a> At 49.1%, turnout was slightly ahead of that for Russia as a whole which was only 47.8%.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://ria.ru/infografika/20160918/1476912507.html#/summary">[3]</a>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2018_Russian_presidential_election" title="2018 Russian presidential election">2018 Russian presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> secured 92% of the vote in Crimea compared to 77% across Russia as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Crimea" title="Demographics of Crimea">Demographics of Crimea</a></div>
<p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Crimea&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the total population of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> was 2,248,400 people (Republic of Crimea: 1,889,485, Sevastopol: 395,000).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> This is down from the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Census_(2001)" title="Ukrainian Census (2001)">2001 Ukrainian Census</a> figure, which was 2,376,000 (Autonomous Republic of Crimea: 2,033,700, Sevastopol: 342,451).<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg/330px-%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg/440px-%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A6%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BA%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%92%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%96%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%A5%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE_%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%81_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Foros_Church" title="Foros Church">Foros Church</a> near Yalta</div></div></div>
<p>According to the 2014 Russian census, 84% of Crimean inhabitants named <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> as their native language; 7.9% – <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">Crimean Tatar</a>; 3.7% – <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a>; and 3.3% – <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  It was the first official Russian census in Crimea since Ukrainian that held in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-dt_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2001 census, 77% of Crimean inhabitants named <a href="/wiki/Russian_language_in_Ukraine" title="Russian language in Ukraine">Russian</a> as their native language; 11.4% – Crimean Tatar; and 10.1% – Ukrainian.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, however, the Crimean Tatar language was estimated to be on the brink of extinction, being taught in Crimea only in around 15 schools at that point. Turkey provided the greatest support to Tatars in Ukraine, which had been unable to resolve the problem of education in their mother tongue in Crimea, by bringing the schools to a modern state.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ethnic composition of Crimea's population has changed dramatically since the early 20th century. The 1897 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">Russian Empire Census</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Taurida_Governorate" title="Taurida Governorate">Taurida Governorate</a> reported: 196,854 (13.06%) Crimean Tatars, 404,463 (27.94%) Russians and 611,121 (42.21%) Ukrainians. But these numbers included Berdyansky, Dneprovsky and Melitopolsky <a href="/wiki/Uyezds" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyezds">uyezds</a> which were on mainland, not in Crimea. The population number excluding these uyezds is given in the table below.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: right; font-size:80%; width=100%">

<tbody><tr style="background:#e0e0e0;" valign="top">
<th rowspan="1">Date
</th>

<p>Crimean Tatars, a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> ethnic minority who in 2001 made up 12.1% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-2001CensusUKRCR_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001CensusUKRCR-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> formed in Crimea in the late <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, after the Crimean Khanate had come into existence. The Crimean Tatars were <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">forcibly expelled</a> to Central Asia by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>'s government as a form of collective punishment, on the grounds that they had formed pro-German <a href="/wiki/Tatar_Legion" class="mw-redirect" title="Tatar Legion">Tatar Legions</a>. After the fall of the Soviet Union, Crimean Tatars began to return to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Census_(2001)" title="Ukrainian Census (2001)">2001 Ukrainian population census</a>, 58% of the population of Crimea are ethnic Russians and 24% are ethnic Ukrainians.<sup id="cite_ref-2001CensusUKRCR_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001CensusUKRCR-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia" title="History of the Jews in Russia">Jews</a> in Crimea were historically <a href="/wiki/Krymchaks" title="Krymchaks">Krymchaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Karaites" title="Crimean Karaites">Karaites</a> (the latter a small group centered at <a href="/wiki/Yevpatoria" title="Yevpatoria">Yevpatoria</a>). The 1879 census for the Taurida Governorate reported a Jewish population of 4.20%, not including a Karaite population of 0.43%.
The Krymchaks (but not the Karaites) were <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Russia" title="The Holocaust in Russia">targeted for annihilation</a> during <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ukraine" title="Reichskommissariat Ukraine">Nazi occupation</a>.
</p><p>The number of <a href="/wiki/Crimea_Germans" title="Crimea Germans">Crimea Germans</a> was 60,000 in 1939. During WWII, they were forcibly deported on the orders of Stalin, as they were regarded as a potential "fifth column".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> This was part of the 800,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germans_in_Russia,_Ukraine_and_the_Soviet_Union" title="History of Germans in Russia, Ukraine and the Soviet Union">Germans in Russia</a> who were relocated within the Soviet Union during Stalinist times.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The 2001 Ukrainian census reports just 2,500 ethnic Germans (0.1% of population) in Crimea.
</p><p>Besides the Crimean Germans, Stalin in 1944 also deported 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, 14,000 Bulgarians<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Italians_of_Crimea" title="Italians of Crimea">Italians</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:RosyBrown"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 93.906250581749px; border-left-color:Yellow"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 72.654252800536px; border-left-color:Black"></div>

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Black"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 54.975465219277px; border-left-color:Honeydew"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Honeydew"></div>

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:48.175367410172px 87.630668004386px 0 0; border-top-color:DarkOrchid"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Crimea (2013)<sup id="cite_ref-2013survey_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013survey-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Orthodox</a> (58%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> (15%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Belief without religion (10%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheist</a> (2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religion (2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:RosyBrown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Not stated (13%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>In 2013, Orthodox Christians made up 58% of the Crimean population, followed by Muslims (15%) and believers in God without religion (10%).<sup id="cite_ref-2013survey_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013survey-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2014_Russian_annexation_of_Crimea" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Russian annexation of Crimea">2014 Russian annexation of Crimea</a> 38 out of 46 the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_%E2%80%93_Kiev_Patriarchate" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church – Kiev Patriarchate">Ukrainian Orthodox Church – Kiev Patriarchate</a> parishes in Crimea ceased to exist, in three cases churches were seized by the Russian authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Notwithstanding the annexation the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_(Moscow_Patriarchate)" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Moscow Patriarchate)">Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Moscow Patriarchate)</a> kept control of its <a href="/wiki/Eparchies" class="mw-redirect" title="Eparchies">eparchies</a> in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
