href="/wiki/File:1837._%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%88%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%85%D1%87%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%B4%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%B5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a> in Bakhchisaray Palace.  Painting by <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Chernetsov" title="Grigory Chernetsov">Grigory Chernetsov</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a> visited <a href="/wiki/Bakhchysarai" title="Bakhchysarai">Bakhchysarai</a> in 1820 and later wrote the poem <a href="/wiki/The_Fountain_of_Bakhchisaray" title="The Fountain of Bakhchisaray">The Fountain of Bakhchisaray</a>. Crimea was the background for <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz" title="Adam Mickiewicz">Adam Mickiewicz</a>'s seminal work, <a href="/wiki/The_Crimean_Sonnets" title="The Crimean Sonnets">The Crimean Sonnets</a> inspired by his 1825 travel. A series of 18 <a href="/wiki/Sonnets" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonnets">sonnets</a> constitute an artistic telling of a journey to and through the Crimea, they feature romantic descriptions of the oriental nature and culture of the East which show the despair of an exile longing for the homeland, driven from his home by a violent enemy.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ivan_Aivazovsky" title="Ivan Aivazovsky">Ivan Aivazovsky</a>, the 19th-century marine painter of Armenian origin, who is considered one of the major artists of his era was born in <a href="/wiki/Feodosia" title="Feodosia">Feodosia</a> and lived there for the most part of his life. Many of his paintings depict the Black Sea. He also created battle paintings during the Crimean War.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Crimean Tatar singer <a href="/wiki/Jamala" title="Jamala">Jamala</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2016" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2016">Eurovision Song Contest 2016</a> representing Ukraine with her song <a href="/wiki/1944_(song)" title="1944 (song)">1944</a>, about the historic deportation of Crimean Tatars in that year by Soviet authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the, broken in practice by Russian companies, Ukrainian “law on concert activities” only Ukrainian companies can organise concerts in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_status_referendum" title="2014 Crimean status referendum">Crimea's vote to join Russia</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation</a> in March 2014, the top football clubs withdrew from the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_football_league_system" title="Ukrainian football league system">Ukrainian leagues</a>. Some clubs registered to join the Russian leagues but the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Federation of Ukraine">Football Federation of Ukraine</a> objected. <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> ruled that Crimean clubs could not join the Russian leagues but should instead be part of a Crimean league system. The <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Premier_League" title="Crimean Premier League">Crimean Premier League</a> is now the top professional football league in Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of Crimean-born athletes have been given permission to compete for Russia instead of Ukraine at future competitions, including <a href="/wiki/Vera_Rebrik" title="Vera Rebrik">Vera Rebrik</a>, the European javelin champion.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_Russia" title="Doping in Russia">Russia currently being suspended from all international athletic competitions</a> Rebrik participates in tournaments as a "neutral" athlete.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Tokarev, Alexey (2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160112111331/http://www.vestnik.mgimo.ru/sites/default/files/pdf/004_istoriya_tokarevaa.pdf">"Archived copy" <bdi lang="ru">Электоральная история постсоветского Крыма: от УССР до России</bdi></a> &#91;The electoral history of the post-Soviet Crimea: from Ukrainian SSR to Russia&#93; <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>MGIMO Review of International Relations</i> (in Russian). <b>5</b> (44): 32–41. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vestnik.mgimo.ru/sites/default/files/pdf/004_istoriya_tokarevaa.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2016-01-12<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2017-08-11</span></span>. <q>Спустя 22 года и 364 дня после первого в СССР референдума в автономной республике Украины Крым состоялся последний референдум. Проводился он вопреки украинскому законодательству, не предусматривающему понятия региональный референдум и предписывающему решать территориальные вопросы только на всеукраинском референдуме</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=MGIMO+Review+of+International+Relations&amp;rft.atitle=Archived+copy+%D0%AD%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE+%D0%9A%D1%80%D1%8B%D0%BC%D0%B0%3A+%D0%BE%D1%82+%D0%A3%D0%A1%D0%A1%D0%A0+%D0%B4%D0%BE+%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8&amp;rft.volume=5&amp;rft.issue=44&amp;rft.pages=32-41&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.aulast=Tokarev&amp;rft.aufirst=Alexey&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.vestnik.mgimo.ru%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Fpdf%2F004_istoriya_tokarevaa.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACrimea" class="Z3988"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment">CS1 maint: archived copy as title (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_archived_copy_as_title" title="Category:CS1 maint: archived copy as title">link</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Marxen, Christian (2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.zaoerv.de/74_2014/74_2014_2_a_367_392.pdf">"The Crimea Crisis – An International Law Perspective"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Zeitschrift für ausländisches öffentliches Recht und Völkerrecht (Heidelberg Journal of International Law)</i>. <b>74</b>. <q>Organizing and holding the referendum on Crimea's accession to Russia was illegal under the Ukrainian constitution. Article 2 of the constitution establishes that "Ukraine shall be a unitary state" and that the "territory of Ukraine within its present border is indivisible and inviolable". This is confirmed in regard to Crimea by Chapter X of the constitution, which provides for the autonomous status of Crimea. Article 134 sets forth that Crimea is an "inseparable constituent part of Ukraine". The autonomous status provides Crimea with a certain set of authorities and allows, inter alia, to hold referendums. These rights are, however, limited to local matters. The constitution makes clear that alterations to the territory of Ukraine require an all-Ukrainian referendum.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Zeitschrift+f%C3%BCr+ausl%C3%A4ndisches+%C3%B6ffentliches+Recht+und+V%C3%B6lkerrecht+%28Heidelberg+Journal+of+International+Law%29&amp;rft.atitle=The+Crimea+Crisis+%E2%80%93+An+International+Law+Perspective&amp;rft.volume=74&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.aulast=Marxen&amp;rft.aufirst=Christian&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.zaoerv.de%2F74_2014%2F74_2014_2_a_367_392.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACrimea" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

"it was indeed at some point between the 1730s and the 1770s that the dream of recreating ancient 'Taurida' in the southern Crimea was conceived. <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine</a>'s plan was to create a paradisiacal imperial 'garden' there, and her Greek archbishop <a href="/wiki/Eugenios_Voulgaris" title="Eugenios Voulgaris">Eugenios Voulgaris</a> obliged by inventing a new etymology for the old name of Tauris, deriving it from <i>taphros</i>, which (he claimed) was the ancient Greek for a ditch dug by human hands."</span>
